<UserId.>107359231467766419114</UserId.>< user_name>

<time>1525037372661</time><Rating>4< /Rating><Review>This is a unique Starbucks just outside the SFO airport off Old Bayshore Highway with an ocean view of planes landing and taking off. It's located inside the Marriott hotel and isn't easily accessible to the public, unless one is willing to pay the Marriott parking costs ($7-23) or park in the street and walk 10-15 minutes. Prices are steeper than normal Starbucks (around 20-30% more than normal) but that's part of the cost for the unique location. It's also "special" in its own way in that they don't offer typical Starbucks refills and instead only refill hot coffee drinks.

Other than that, it's a very nice spot with comfortable indoor and outdoor seating. WiFi was adequate too, freely provided by Marriott with 2Mbps down and up.

I ordered a trenta strawberry acai for $6.21 that normally costs $4.72 and found it be consistent with other Starbucks.<//Review>< Pictures>

< Text>
It's a great place for typical consumers to get tools and equipment at generally very low prices. It's not a place for most professionals and business that will heavily use the tools or put them through hard tests. Many times as a typical consumer you only need some equipment for a specific project or task and may only use it again every few months or years. This place will usually have what you need. Be aware that not everything is a great deal, especially when you consider quality, value, and durability, but I've generally been pleased.<//Text>

<user_id>108190533373010836933</user_id>< review>
Low price tools! The majority of which have lifetime warranty so long as they are hand tools. Most of the electronic type tools are 90-day limited warranty. The employees here super chill and will help you find what you're looking for. Lots of people use this place as a tool rental place: Essentially buy what you need to get the job done and then return it and get your money back! Kind of screwed up but it's not against their policy lol. The line of tools by baauer: such as impacts & hammer drills and stuff like that, are actually pretty damn good, give Makita a run for their money @ a fraction of the price.</review>

< text>
The positives:
They're responsive and kind when you speak on the phone and offer help or will send someone out right away.

If an appliance stops working they work to get you a new one fairly easily. Had a fridge go out and they replaced it with one that was too big but helped get the right one in there.

They got a new laundry machine when the one that barely worked broke down.

Keith and Perla are very kind people, always easy to work with and helpful, but see below for the negatives on the move out as that was where I feel they felt short.

The negatives:
They hire the cheapest contractors they can find and the contractors they hire won't do the work right or well. (Had a carport leak that dropped residue constantly on my new car when it rained, they didn't fix it right as the grating didn't fit in the drain, and it still leaked)

Laundry machines on site were terrible, and I mean terrible. I've lived in a lot of apartments and I've never experienced such poor laundry machines. It costs you about 5-6 dollars in quarters just to do the laundry and end up with it damp.

The cleanliness when I moved in was disgusting, but I needed a place and didn't complain about it at the time. (Pee below the toilet, a dirty shower, oven still had stuff in it etc)

The moving out process was the most uptight I've ever seen especially given the above statement on the cleanliness upon moving in. I went around the house with my girlfriend for hours filling every tack hole (yes tiny little tack holes that you couldn't even make out half the time) because of the complaint that holes hadn't been filled. Getting my deposit back I was deducted based upon that.

I also was deducted based upon touch up paint and minor scuffs which in any other apartment falls under the normal wear and tear so this came as a surprise to me because I've never been charged for something of that sort. Also the way they like to paint things is by just painting over old peeled paint and not sanding it and doing it correctly therefore making it easier for it to degrade.

The other surprise to me was that they called out that they had to replace items that weren't there when I moved in such as a tub stopper. (The tub has a valve switch to plug and unplug the drain which didnt work upon moving in but that's besides the point).

Apparently it took someone two hours to fill pinholes and paint minor wear which also is a surprise to me.

Overall I'd rate experience living in the apartment as fine and acceptable. The moving out part was the worst move out experience I've had.

Honestly look somewhere else if you'd like to have someone who will repair your issues correctly. And unless you like losing a chunk of your already ridiculous deposit to superficial things mentioned above then I recommend looking elsewhere.</text>

<Text>Last fall DeDe's was recommended to me by the real estate agent who was helping me buy rental properties. I made an appointment with Keith Becker (owner/president) and we discussed what I was looking for in rents and tenants (families), he showed me the contract he has with the landlords and asked about the insurance I have for the properties. He told me that the company would conduct an inspection before the property was rented (and once a year after that) in order to determine what kinds of repairs would be necessary for "habitability".  He assigned my properties to agent Jenny Rihl.
Jenny did a walk thru with me for each of the properties.  She informed me of some repairs that were safety issues that I hadn't considered. Jenny arranged for the work to be done, either with in-house workers or outside vendors. She also set up ongoing yard maintenance. She cleared every repair with me. She put the properties on the rental market as they were repaired, and when she had applications from tenants, she presented them to me. I had such a great experience dress shopping here. The Bridal and Tuxedo Galleria has a seemingly endless amount of styles to try. My consultant was Kayla, and she was absolutely fantastic. She communicated with me prior to the appointment for my vision so she could pull styles ahead of my appointment. Additionally, during the appointment, Kayla was extremely attentive and really listened to what I did and didn't like about each dress. Fourth, the lady helping was nice herself, however she only could get me size 10s and was trying to force them onto me saying she could try to pin it or I should hold up the top to get the style. I told her I couldn't even get a good idea since I was just holding it up. When they didn't fit, I feel like she started to panic and was just finding ANY dress that could fit. I was able to try ONE size 12 dress that fit, however that was it. She was just trying to sell me a dress, not trying to find my dress.

It doesn't make any sense to me to only have size 10s and below for dresses. Which is fine, however then you should indicate that on your website that you only have samples that are 8-10.

If you are a 25 year old, at most a size 8, and on a tight budget, you will probably have good luck finding a dress. But try going to a real boutique and you will have a completely different experience. Luckily earlier that day I went to another boutique and had an incredibly awesome experience so this one didn't ruin my day. I had a private room for myself and the girls, the sales lady sat down and looked at my pictures and then went to gather the dresses and helped me put them on. ALL of them fit with clamps on the back for excess materials.

Good luck and I hope you at least go to another boutique for a real experience!<//Text><username>Carol Deak< /username><Date>1467071575117</Date><pics>None< /pics>< response>

< user_name>
Scott Miller< /user_name>
< text>
I moved to North County 9 years ago and happily found this place, it was good, 9 years ago. The place has gone down hill ever since in food quality, quantity and service only going up a steep hill in price. Today was, sad to say, definitely  my last visit. I have never received a smile here. Today was the first time I got my toast WITH breakfast instead of for desert but dang, it was burnt and really, really small. My daughters french toast was smaller than a slice of wonder bread. My complete breakfast was NOT GOOD. It took over 40 min. for us to get our food and our order was the only one for the kitchen at the time. "Regulars" seem to be treated better than the average joe as evidenced by today's regulars Buddy the bulldog and his owner whom were served immediately upon entering the restaurant. Yes, Buddy the dog was served dog food from behind the counter in the restaurant (Buddy probably ate the best of anyone there today). The current stone faced waitress whom has been there for a long time as far as I can remember, is bouncing all over the place looking busy enough yet nothing is really happening, except the dog is getting stellar service on the floor from her (we were stuck there for over an hour mainly waiting for food and the check) and with all the activity by the waitress feeding, petting the dog etc. I never once saw the waitress wash her hands!
So, a couple of flavorless eggs, cold undercooked sausage, burnt, mini, dry sourdough toast (they don't butter it for you) and mushy, starchy hashbrowns along with mini french toast, a cup of coffee, an orange juice from a carton and "dirty" service for $25.00 without so much as a thank you of even a smile?
THANKS BUT NO THANKS.< /text>

< review>
I have been going to 101 for breakfast on sundays for the last year.  At first it was good but has steadily gone downhill in the last 6mos.  They don't cook with much seasoning so you have to really salt and pepper everything heavily.  The gravy is like tasteless paste.  Now they have started cutting back the portions and charging anywhere from 50c to 70c just to put a little extra gravy on the potatoes, which are dry so they need it.  On the last two visits, I noticed that the portions have been cut in at least half if not more.  I have eaten my last meal there.  It is just not worth the price anymore.< /review>

< Text>
(Translated by Google) This cafeteria seems to be frozen in the 50's and that is what gives it personality. The waiters attend you kindly. The food is simple, unpretentious and with good taste. I ordered 2 fried eggs with potatoes and toast (Solo Cruise in the menu) and it is just what I got. The mural that is outside is very beautiful and inside it is possible to see very old photos of Oceanside. The "diner" takes its name from the California U.S. Route 101 that goes from San Diego to Oregon.

(Original)
Esta cafeteria parece que se quedo congelada en los 50's y eso es le da personalidad. Los meseros te atienden amablemente. La comida es sencilla, sin pretenciones y con buen sabor. Yo pedi 2 huevos estrellados con papas y pan tostado (Solo Cruise en el menu) y es justo lo que obtuve.  El mural que esta afuera es muy bonito y dentro es posible ver fotos muy viejas de Oceanside. El "diner" toma su nombre de la California U.S. Route 101 que va desde San Diego hasta Oregon.<//Text>
